  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a6514b5a-fd27-4a2c-9b9e-1aca171d9350'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer8115540960023010918">Tired of memoirs that only tell you what <i>really</i> happened?<br/><br/>Sick of deeply personal accounts written in the first person? Seeking an exciting, interactive read that puts the “u” back in “aUtobiography”? Then look no further than <i>Neil Patrick Harris: Choose Your Own Autobiography</i>! In this revolutionary, Joycean experiment in light celebrity narrative, actor/personality/carbon-</span>
  <span id="freeText8115540960023010918" style="display:none">Tired of memoirs that only tell you what <i>really</i> happened?<br /><br />Sick of deeply personal accounts written in the first person? Seeking an exciting, interactive read that puts the “u” back in “aUtobiography”? Then look no further than <i>Neil Patrick Harris: Choose Your Own Autobiography</i>! In this revolutionary, Joycean experiment in light celebrity narrative, actor/personality/carbon-based life-form Neil Patrick Harris lets you, the reader, live his life. You will be born in New Mexico. You will get your big break at an acting camp. You will get into a bizarre confrontation outside a nightclub with actor Scott Caan. Even better, at each critical juncture of your life, you will choose how to proceed. You will decide whether to try out for <i>Doogie Howser, M.D.</i> You will decide whether to spend years struggling with your sexuality. You will decide what kind of caviar you want to eat on board Elton John’s yacht.<br /> <br />Choose correctly and you’ll find fame, fortune, and true love. Choose incorrectly and you’ll find misery, heartbreak, and a hideous death by piranhas. All this, plus magic tricks, cocktail recipes, embarrassing pictures from your time as a child actor, and even a closing song. Yes, if you buy one book this year, congratulations on being above the American average, but make that book <i>Neil Patrick Harris: Choose Your Own Autobiography</i>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8115540960023010918" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/218264-has-anyone-tried-this-book-in-audio-form">Has anyone tried this book in audio form? On Audible, the description says 
&quot;hear all of the same fun and humor from the printed version but you don’t have to make any decisions or jump around - just kick back, relax and listen.&quot; However I am wondering will this drastically change my enjoyment of the book versus reading a physical copy?</a>
</div>

<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_218264'><a id="like_count_community_question_218264" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/218264?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">6 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F20170296-neil-patrick-harris">like</a></span>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/37650349-luigi-evangelista"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_100x100-c7bfe730633c9983e27caaa66a8e244a.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/37650349-luigi-evangelista">Luigi Evangelista</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I just picked up the audiobook from the library and it's read by the author himself. Neil usually finishes a story and then gives either 2 or 3 option<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I just picked up the audiobook from the library and it's read by the author himself. Neil usually finishes a story and then gives either 2 or 3 options and he'll say if you choose this, then wait a minute...if you choose this, keep listening and if you choose this, then hang on, it's coming. Spoiler alert-I'm on disc 3 of 6 and he's died horrible deaths on at least 4 occasions so far. There's a special treat when you get to the part where he meets his husband-his other half makes a special appearance in the audiobook as well and it's pretty funny to listen to.<br /><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

I live outside the US (so I don´t have the ability to actually view the book) but want to purchase this book for a friend. I need suggestions on whether to go with the hardcover or take the ereader option. I never know with this sort of more interactive book. Can someone who has read the book or even seen it tell me if the e reader experience would be more positive/negative?</a>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1101716338" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1101716338" />
    <a title="Patrick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/922495-patrick"><img alt="Patrick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351307095p2/922495.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1101716338?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/922495-patrick">Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/922495-patrick?shelf=books-i-would-blurb">books-i-would-blurb</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1101716338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12003944554976188313">I expected this book to be witty. I expected it to be clever and fun. And it was. It was all of those things in spades. <br/><br/>But I didn't expect it to be sweet and sad and honest and touching. I mean, it's framed as a choose-your-own-adventure. You don't expect those to be heartfelt, emotional stories....<br/><br/>Perhaps I should start by saying that I came to know Neil Patrick Harris in a different way than people. Most of you probably know him from his two big TV shows: Doogie Howser or How I Met Your Mothe</span>
  <span id="freeText12003944554976188313" style="display:none">I expected this book to be witty. I expected it to be clever and fun. And it was. It was all of those things in spades. <br /><br />But I didn't expect it to be sweet and sad and honest and touching. I mean, it's framed as a choose-your-own-adventure. You don't expect those to be heartfelt, emotional stories....<br /><br />Perhaps I should start by saying that I came to know Neil Patrick Harris in a different way than people. Most of you probably know him from his two big TV shows: Doogie Howser or How I Met Your Mother. <br /><br />Not so with me. I was aware of those shows, even watched them. But I came to appreciate Harris by watching Undercover Brother. Later, my admiration grew when I saw him play a deranged version of himself in Harold and Kumar. And last I came to love him through Dr. Horrible's Sing-Along Blog. <br /><br />Oddly enough, it was the last of these that shot my respect for his craft as an actor through the roof. (And, to tangent briefly, still makes me think he would do a great job of playing Bast, should my books ever make it to the screen.)<br /><br />I mention this to let you know that I came at this book as a fan, but not as your typical sort of fan. <br /><br />So. The book. Simply said, I loved it. As I mentioned above, it was everything I expected and more. It was funny enough to make my laugh out loud more than once. And sweet enough to make me cry on an airplane twice. <br /><br />Specific things I enjoyed:<br /><br />I liked that he spoke frankly about how he came to grips with the fact that he was gay, as well as the conflict of coming out publicly. It was extraordinary insightful. <br /><br />There are little pieces of the book written by various celebrities Harris has interacted with over the years, Penn Jillette, Sarah Silverman, etc etc. These were lovely, quirky additions to the book. <br /><br />What's more, the Choose-Your-Own-Adventure aspect worked remarkably well. At first I thought it was just a gimmick, but I quickly learned this is a great format for an Autobiography, as it gave me the chance to skip to the parts of the book I was most interested in. Then, later on, I went back and read it again. <br /><br />Simply said, it was a great book. It's the only autobiography I'd be tempted to read again in the future. And it's only one I've ever considered buying multiple copies of as a Christmas gifts. <br /><br />Lastly, speaking as a writer, it was irritatingly well written. It just doesn't doesn't seem fair that Harris should be able to sing, dance, act, AND write this well. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12003944554976188313" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17160678695949637130" style="display:none">Kids, did I ever tell you about the time I read your Uncle Neil's wonderfully weird autobiography? No, not the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4725669.The_Bro_Code" title="The Bro Code by Barney Stinson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bro Code</a>.<br><br><i>♪ Pa pa pa pa, pa pa pa pa...<br>pa pa, da da da da, da da da da da...♪</i><br><br>It was the autumn of 2014 and your Aunt Robin was on a top secret mission for S.H.I.E.L.D. (She was <a href="http://www.imdb.com/name/nm0453115/" rel="nofollow noopener">Taran Killin'</a>* it, by the way.) Anyway, Neil had just released a book that was unlike any other celebrity autobiography before. You see kids, most people use their books to either brag about themselves or garner sympathy for "overcoming a personal tragedy"; Neil just wanted to make you laugh. Also, he wanted you to be a bit jealous of his husband's game.<br><br>Inside that book, you'll find out about his experiences with:<br><br><b>Celebrities</b><br>Interspersed throughout the book are not only tales of NPH’s run-ins with celebs, but also short notes from the famous names themselves. There are plenty of juicy tidbits about other celebs but it’s all a good-natured ribbing (for their pleasure?*). Unless you’re <a href="http://www.imdb.com/name/nm0004790/" rel="nofollow noopener">Scott Caan</a>, in which case I am genuinely mortified for you the same way you get embarrassed about that stupid thing you did in the sixth grade that still keeps you up at night <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Nobody forgot about it and one day you’ll get one of those <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47763.I_Know_What_You_Did_Last_Summer" title="I Know What You Did Last Summer by Lois Duncan" rel="nofollow noopener">I Know What You Did Last Summer</a>-esque notes in the mail  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><br><b>Stage</b><br>Besides doing <i>Rent</i> and being told off by Patti LuPone <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414511445ra/11661459.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<i>And then storm clouds gathered above<br>Into great balls of fire<br>And then fire shot down<br>From the sky in bolts<br>Like shining blades<br>Of a knife.</i><br>- <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VZtyFQQPnEs" rel="nofollow noopener"><b>Origin of Love<b></b></b></a>

Fun Fact: Baby Bop did the laughter for Nicki Minaj's classic <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=LDZX4ooRsWs" rel="nofollow noopener">Anaconda</a> (uncredited).</i><br><br><b>Mmmmmmmagic!</b><br>Despite being President of the Board of Directors of Hollywood's Magic Castle and having stayed in a presumably haunted landmark, Harris doesn’t believe in the supernatural. There is a part of me that thinks NPH doth protest too much. That perpetually youthful appearance? I’m not going to play TMZ’s “Good Genes or Good Docs” game here; I’m just going to go ahead and say it: Harris is some sort of elven creature. While reading the book you become aware of his statistically impossible streak of good luck and he <i>does</i> have an impish sense of humor so perhaps he’s some sort of leprechaun??<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414510603ra/11661375.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And that, kids, is what I thought of his book.<br><br>BTW, Neil: “Kungaloosh”<br><br>[<i>Straightens tie, vanishes in puff of smoke</i>]<br><br><br>*See what I did there?</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3047955812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2408097322498668165"><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576529128i/28622964._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> </blockquote>Ahh...Quaint childhood, a few lucky breaks and then success, success, success.<br/><br/><b>The classic celebrity memoir..<i>.or is it?</i></b><blockquote>
  <i>You come in weighing a very average, very sexy seven pounds, seven ounces. As it happens, that is also the exact weight of an Emmy Award. Coincidence? Yes … but true fact? No.</i>
</blockquote>What if memoirs didn't have to be all filmographies, name-dropping and dry parental issues? <br/><br/>What if...you could pick out what happens yourself?<br/><br/>Well...that sounds like a rather good idea after all...<blockquote>
  </blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText2408097322498668165" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576529128i/28622964._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </blockquote>Ahh...Quaint childhood, a few lucky breaks and then success, success, success.<br><br><b>The classic celebrity memoir..<i>.or is it?</i></b><blockquote>
  <i>You come in weighing a very average, very sexy seven pounds, seven ounces. As it happens, that is also the exact weight of an Emmy Award. Coincidence? Yes … but true fact? No.</i>
</blockquote>What if memoirs didn't have to be all filmographies, name-dropping and dry parental issues? <br><br>What if...you could pick out what happens yourself?<br><br>Well...that sounds like a rather good idea after all...<blockquote>
  <i>So pluck up your courage and take that risk! Add another story to the book of your life. Even if it doesn’t go the way you planned or wanted, you’ll still learn from it. Adventure</i>
</blockquote>Overall - this was an <b>incredibly fun memoir. </b><br><br>I knew of NPH from his HIMYM (How I Met Your Mother) days and absolutely loved his over-the-top character...but I was always curious<b> where the acting stopped and where he began. </b><br><br>This memoir has that covered! I learned so much about his life and various adventures - some real, some imagined.<br><br>I listened to the audiobook version, so I didn't truly have a choose-your-own-adventure vibe from it but I still had fun.<br><br>There were <b>a few twists and turns</b> (dead-ends!) sprinkled in that made it all the more enjoyable. <blockquote>
  <i>But magic is like pizza: even when it's bad, it's pretty good.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>All in all, I was so happy to spend my time listening to this book!<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar">Kelly (and the Book Boar)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer951792503" class="readable"
              >

  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414430957ra/11653453.gif' alt='Commercial Photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Buckle up friends ‘cause this might be a long one . . . Where do I even begin???? I guess I should take my inspiration from NPH and sit down at the computer in order to journal my feelings:<br/><br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414430957ra/11653454.gif' alt='Commercial Photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Let me start by saying you kind of have to be a NPH Fangirl to <i>really</i> appreciate this book. Although funny, Neil’s sto</span>
  <span id="freeText3333246121626629344" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>How can I describe my feelings about my experience with <i>Choose Your Own Autobiography</i>???? Well, this pretty much sums it up:<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414430957ra/11653453.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Buckle up friends ‘cause this might be a long one . . . Where do I even begin???? I guess I should take my inspiration from NPH and sit down at the computer in order to journal my feelings:<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414430957ra/11653454.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Let me start by saying you kind of have to be a NPH Fangirl to <i>really</i> appreciate this book. Although funny, Neil’s story focuses more on the actual <b>story</b> of his life rather than the hardiest of har-har anecdotal moments. Luckily for me I <b>am</b> a superfan and spent the better part of the summer attempting to score a free copy of <i>Choose Your Own Autobiography</i>. Guess what??? Persistence (and the fact that I confessed I was willing to do <i>anything</i> for a freebie) paid off and I was totally able to “get inside” NPH, if you will . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414430957ra/11653455.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And what did I learn that I didn’t know before? A lot. Neil Patrick Harris is so open about . . . well, everything. Not only does he tell you about his entire career from his start as Doogie Howser, M.D. . . .<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414430957ra/11653456.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>FYI - I totally wanted to bang Doogie when I was a kid and received <b>massive</b> amounts of flack for it. I obviously knew what he was going to grow into<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414430957i/11653457._SY540_.jpg" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>(Mommy likey!!!!)<br><br>to box office failure (but massive success in the pop culture arena) . . .<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414430957ra/11653458.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>to massive success on the big screen . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414430957ra/11653459.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>to the weirdest little blog with the biggest following in the history of ever . . .<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414430957ra/11653460.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>to a return to network television in one of the most wildly popular shows (with a completely less-than-stellar ending) . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414430957ra/11653461.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>to triumph and a Tony about one angry little inch . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414430957ra/11653462.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Neil Patrick Harris has done it (and talks about it) all. Including dishing on all of the D-listers of Hollywood who have shown themselves to be d-bags (Doherty, Screech, Anne Heche, Kelsey Grammar, Scott Caan (Who???? Wait, am I the only person in the world who didn’t know not only this guy’s name but that he’s James Caan’s son???? I’ll just crawl back under my rock now).<br><br>Not only does NPH discuss his professional life, but he talks about everything else as well. He’s awesomely self-deprecating (especially when it comes to describing matters of the “heart,” if you will). From his sexuality to family to drug usage (easy there, killer, he was never a Lindsay Blowhan - he merely dabbled), he talks about every aspect of his life. He even throws in some card tricks and a couple of food and cocktail recipes for good measure. He SERIOUSLY covers his life story – I mean all the way up to the Heineken commercials which only began airing a few months ago. And he speaks of his parents, his partner David, and his children with such complete adoration that it almost made rain fall out of my face.<br><br>So, how did <b>my</b> adventure end? Wellllllll . . . after I found myself in a twisted plotline involving murder and decapitation of hitchhikers I figured I better start over and read the book from the beginning so that’s just what I did. Cover to cover. And now??? <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414430957ra/11653463.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Neil Patrick Harris’ story was <b>LEGEN</b><br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414430957ra/11653464.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>DARY!!!!</b><br><br><i>ARC provided by Blogging for Books in exchange for an honest review</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3333246121626629344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_951798053" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/951798053" />
    <a title="Diane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/279256-diane"><img alt="Diane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1497365060p2/279256.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/951798053?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane" href="/user/show/279256-diane">Diane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/279256-diane?shelf=hollywood">hollywood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/279256-diane?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/279256-diane?shelf=memoirs">memoirs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/279256-diane?shelf=humorous">humorous</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer951798053" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15195115208691030411">Hi, my name is Diane and I am a recovering theater addict.<br/><br/>(Group: Hi, Diane.)<br/><br/>I've long been a fan of Neil Patrick Harris. The guy can sing, dance, act funny or serious, and he makes hosting award shows look easy. He's a quintuple threat.<br/><br/>Reading NPH's memoir, it felt like I grew up with him. As a kid, he loved the musical "Annie" and memorized the choreography. I also loved Annie and used to drive my mom nuts singing "It's a hard knock life."<br/><br/>NPH was blown away by the show "Les Misérables," callin</span>
  <span id="freeText15195115208691030411" style="display:none">Hi, my name is Diane and I am a recovering theater addict.<br /><br />(Group: Hi, Diane.)<br /><br />I've long been a fan of Neil Patrick Harris. The guy can sing, dance, act funny or serious, and he makes hosting award shows look easy. He's a quintuple threat.<br /><br />Reading NPH's memoir, it felt like I grew up with him. As a kid, he loved the musical "Annie" and memorized the choreography. I also loved Annie and used to drive my mom nuts singing "It's a hard knock life."<br /><br />NPH was blown away by the show "Les Misérables," calling it a "phenomenal, transcendent experience." Les Miz is my favorite musical and I am in crazy love with the soundtrack.<br /><br />He acted in a bunch of community theater productions in his hometown. So did I. <br /><br />As a teenager, he starred in the TV show "Doogie Howser, M.D." I used to watch Doogie.<br /><br />Neil said a pivotal event of his life was starring in a touring production of "Rent." "When you act in Rent you have to own its ideals: no day but today; forget regret or life is yours to miss; there's only us, there's only this. You instantly embrace the beautiful worldview of the show."<br /><br />I loved "Rent" and would pay big bucks (or what was a big bucks to a college student) to see the show whenever it toured through my city. I also have the soundtrack memorized.<br /><br />Neil is a fan of Joss Whedon and starred in one of the most wonderful things ever to be on the web, "Dr. Horrible's Sing-Along Blog." I <i>lovelovelove</i> Joss Whedon and, yes, I regularly listen to the Dr. Horrible soundtrack. <br /><br />In short, this NPH memoir was perfect for me and helped me break out of a reading slump. I listened to this on audio, and as expected, Neil is an excellent narrator. If you haven't seen a printed copy, he did this fun gimmick where he borrowed the style of the Choose Your Own Adventure books (which I also loved as a kid) and it gives you a chance to make choices about what section to read next. (In audio, Neil basically read the book in sequence, and he adapted the choices at the end of each chapter by saying something like, if you want to host the Emmys, wait a little bit. If you want to star in a network TV show, keep reading!) <br /><br />Neil is a very funny guy. I frequently laughed out loud while listening to his stories. I am such a theater dork that I loved hearing the behind-the-scenes stuff about the different Broadway shows he's been in, or even his process for hosting an award show. Frequently I paused my reading to go watch videos online of whatever story he just told. <br /><br />The book is also poignant, especially when Neil writes about becoming a father, or his feelings about being an openly gay man in Hollywood. <br /><br />"You have seen instances when the hard-core vehemence of some gay-rights activists creates a backlash, making homophobes even more homophobic. For you it all goes back to the fundamental rule of creative endeavor, and life is if nothing else a creative endeavor: Show, don't tell. Personal confidence, ease, conducting yourself publicly with grace and humility — these are the qualities you consider most effective. Directly showing family and neighbors and co-workers that you're proud of the way you live accomplishes something on a core level that intense advocacy sometimes can't."<br /><br />This is a thoughtful and delightful memoir, and I would recommend it to fellow NPH fans. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15195115208691030411" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11517226842464021051"><b>HILARIOUS AND YET VERY REAL</b><br/><br/>✨ Popsugar Reading Challenge 2019✨ <br/>✨✨A "choose-your-own-adventure" book✨✨<br/><br/>What can I say about this book? Maybe I should give the word to one of the author's close friends, Mr. Barney Stinson:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1572729657ra/28393753.gif' width='400' height='auto' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>👍 THE THINGS I LIKED 👍</b><br/><br/><u>Personality</u>: Usually autobiography are weirdly devoid of personality, in my opinion at least. They are this weird politically correct things, that almost dehumanise their subjects. The truly refreshing thing about this autobiography was how clearly NPH's perso</span>
  <span id="freeText11517226842464021051" style="display:none"><b>HILARIOUS AND YET VERY REAL</b><br><br>✨ Popsugar Reading Challenge 2019✨ <br>✨✨A "choose-your-own-adventure" book✨✨<br><br>What can I say about this book? Maybe I should give the word to one of the author's close friends, Mr. Barney Stinson:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1572729657ra/28393753.gif" width="400" height="auto" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>👍 THE THINGS I LIKED 👍</b><br><br><u>Personality</u>: Usually autobiography are weirdly devoid of personality, in my opinion at least. They are this weird politically correct things, that almost dehumanise their subjects. The truly refreshing thing about this autobiography was how clearly NPH's personality shone through. Honestly, it almost felt like it smacked me in the face. And I loved it.<br><br><u>Fun</u>: Again, not a word I would usually associate with autobiographies. But this was so humorous and innovative in the writing and the telling that I could not help but to fall in love with it.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Admission is free and worth every penny."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><u>Barney</u>: As, arguably, NPH's most famous role, Barney Stinson of course makes and appearance or two throughout the book. Being a big HIMYM-fan, that was greatly appreciated!<br><br><u>Honesty</u>: Even thought the tone of this book was largely comedic, it was also very honest and candid. I really felt like I got to peek behind the curtains into the inner sanctum of NPH.<br><br>Follow me for more book goodness: <a href="https://www.facebook.com/BibliophiliaDK/?modal=admin_todo_tour" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/BibliophiliaDK" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/bibliophiliadk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>

<div id="review_2622317549" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2622317549" />
    <a title="Jenna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3536004-jenna"><img alt="Jenna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535136437p2/3536004.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2622317549?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenna" href="/user/show/3536004-jenna">Jenna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jenna by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/35088694-carly-friedman">Carly Friedman</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3536004-jenna?shelf=memoir-biography">memoir-biography</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3536004-jenna?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3536004-jenna?shelf=humour">humour</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2622317549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11789341139760337152">Cute and quirky, <i>Neil Patrick Harris: Choose Your Own Autobiography​</i> is a light-hearted and funny autobiography. Remember those choose-your-own-ending books? This is written in that style. It is a very different concept for an autobiography and I could have done without that for the very simple reason that those books always make me anxious! I worry that I'll miss something if I do the "choose-your-own" thing -- I won't get to read every single page and miss something important. I also worry tha</span>
  <span id="freeText11789341139760337152" style="display:none">Cute and quirky, <i>Neil Patrick Harris: Choose Your Own Autobiography​</i> is a light-hearted and funny autobiography. Remember those choose-your-own-ending books? This is written in that style. It is a very different concept for an autobiography and I could have done without that for the very simple reason that those books always make me anxious! I worry that I'll miss something if I do the "choose-your-own" thing -- I won't get to read every single page and miss something important. I also worry that if I read it cover to cover like a regular book, I'll miss something! One solution to that would be to keep re-reading until I've exhausted all the possible options... but I think I'd grow bored very quickly! And so, I read this cover to cover, one time. It was fun and I did enjoy the humourous choices given, in spite of feeling anxious about possibly missing something.<br /><br />Neil Patrick Harris presents as a very likable person, very sweet, kind, and funny. He's never been my favourite actor because I don't like the shows I've seen him in, but I like him more having read this book. He talks about his childhood (giving an alternate version in case someone wants to read about awful parents!), his career, his husband, and his children. There are some cute drawings in the book, as well as a few recipes, card tricks, and letters written by various celebrities to and about Neil. Worth reading if you enjoy auto-/biographies.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11789341139760337152" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1103881817" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10358687033792996977"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472750173i/20237706._SX540_.jpg' width='200' height='150' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b> I am charmed.</b><br/><br/>I'm a big NPH fan going all the way back to his Doogie Howser days, so I was really excited to listen to this audiobook. <br/><br/>Though the format was a little strange for audio (choose your own adventure works less well when you are listening linearly), it worked well enough. And <b>I <i>promise</i> you that you will leave this audiobook feeling a kinship with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/620872.Neil_Patrick_Harris' title='Neil Patrick Harris' rel='nofollow noopener'>Neil Patrick Harris</a> in one way or another. </b><br/><br/>I loved all of the <b>intimate details,</b> that we got about his life, from his journey in self-discove</span>
  <span id="freeText10358687033792996977" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472750173i/20237706._SX540_.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> I am charmed.</b><br><br>I'm a big NPH fan going all the way back to his Doogie Howser days, so I was really excited to listen to this audiobook. <br><br>Though the format was a little strange for audio (choose your own adventure works less well when you are listening linearly), it worked well enough. And <b>I <i>promise</i> you that you will leave this audiobook feeling a kinship with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/620872.Neil_Patrick_Harris" title="Neil Patrick Harris" rel="nofollow noopener">Neil Patrick Harris</a> in one way or another. </b><br><br>I loved all of the <b>intimate details,</b> that we got about his life, from his journey in self-discovery of his sexuality, to hearing about his relationship with the theater, to his love of magic (though I'll admit to skimming some of the magic trick clips), to his childhood, and last but not least, his loving relationship with his husband and kids. I laughed and cried along with NPH, and <b>I felt like I gained a friend during the listening experience</b>. <br><br>Not surprisingly, NPH is also a great narrator, with a voice that feels familiar and emotional. He did an excellent job narrating this book, and I sort of wish he narrated other audiobooks too, just so I could keep hearing his voice. <br><br>An easy, fun listen, and an extremely satisfying audio experience. </span>

<div id="review_1087690627" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1087690627" />
    <a title="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books"><img alt="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415550632p2/5892196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1087690627?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" href="/user/show/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books">Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=blogging-for-books">blogging-for-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=own-physical-copy">own-physical-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1087690627" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9066924554142562544">This review can also be found at <a href='http://carolesrandomlife.blogspot.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Carole's Random Life</a>.<br/><br/>This book brings back a lot of fond memories for me. I used to adore reading the choose your own adventure books as a child although I would never choose the right option and always ended up dying of thirst or some other horrible death. I would eventually give up on my ability to make the right choices and try to figure out what I needed to choose by working backwards in the book. Despite my poor decision making skills, I never gave up on the</span>
  <span id="freeText9066924554142562544" style="display:none">This review can also be found at <a href="http://carolesrandomlife.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Carole's Random Life</a>.<br /><br />This book brings back a lot of fond memories for me. I used to adore reading the choose your own adventure books as a child although I would never choose the right option and always ended up dying of thirst or some other horrible death. I would eventually give up on my ability to make the right choices and try to figure out what I needed to choose by working backwards in the book. Despite my poor decision making skills, I never gave up on these books. Every time I brought home a Scholastic flyer from school, I would end up picking out another one of those books. I am the same age as Mr. Harris so it makes some sense that he would fondly remember these books as well as I do and I just love the fact that he used this approach in this book.<br /> <br />There is just something about Neil Patrick Harris that seems to be almost universally appealing. I am not a biography reader. I probably read a few back in high school and college because I had to but I can't think of a time where I picked one up to read for entertainment as an adult....but I wanted to read this book as soon as I heard about it. I am not exactly sure what I find so entertaining about Mr. Harris. Sure I have watched and enjoyed some of his work. His portrayal of Barney Stinsen is...wait for it....legendary. I loved him in Harold and Kumar Go to White Castle. I just have never considered myself to be a huge fan though. If he is on, I'll certainly watch him but I don't go out of my way to be sure to catch him either. I still knew that I had to read this book because there is just something about the way that he tells a story.<br /><br />One thing that I think is genius about this book is the fact that I will certainly be picking it up quite a few more times. It is a choose your own adventure so you have to read it several times just to make sure that you have read every option available. This is a book that I recommend reading as intended with all of the jumping around and choices because it just makes it so much fun. I have been through quite a few options so far with a few ending in a less than ideal manner. I don't think that the book would be nearly as appealing if it were to be read cover to cover.<br /><br />Neil Patrick Harris does have an interesting story to tell. He is a child star that I will always think of as Doogie to some extent. He also talks about his sexuality, his family, and all the things that make him who he is. Some of the parts in the book are simply silly and I liked those just as much as anything else. The book itself looks wonderful. I just love the cover and the section in the center of the book filled with photos is nice to have. <br /><br />I would recommend this book to others. It is witty, funny, touching, and sometimes thought provoking. Plus it is just a lot of fun! This is the first book by Neil Patrick Harris that I have read but I look forward to see what kind of original spin he might apply to a novel in the future.<br /><br /><i>I received a copy of this book from Blogging for Books for the purpose of providing an honest review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9066924554142562544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1110296625" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1110296625" />
    <a title="Jillian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7357386-jillian"><img alt="Jillian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598880595p2/7357386.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1110296625?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jillian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jillian" href="/user/show/7357386-jillian">Jillian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7357386-jillian?shelf=biography-memoir-autobiography">biography-memoir-autobiography</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7357386-jillian?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7357386-jillian?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7357386-jillian?shelf=nostalgia">nostalgia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1110296625" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14535355528853518887">I am torn about this book. I have procrastinated rating this book and writing this review because I am really very sad about reaching the conclusion I have come to.<br/><br/>Usually if I abandon a book, it automatically gets one star because if I can't finish a book, well, that kind of says it all. With this book, I can't do that. My dislike and inability to finish this book were not due to the content or writing style, it was due to the format.<br/><br/>While I very much enjoyed the idea of the nostalgic nature of</span>
  <span id="freeText14535355528853518887" style="display:none">I am torn about this book. I have procrastinated rating this book and writing this review because I am really very sad about reaching the conclusion I have come to.<br /><br />Usually if I abandon a book, it automatically gets one star because if I can't finish a book, well, that kind of says it all. With this book, I can't do that. My dislike and inability to finish this book were not due to the content or writing style, it was due to the format.<br /><br />While I very much enjoyed the idea of the nostalgic nature of the Choose Your Own Adventure format (which falls right into happy memories from my childhood--I am basically NPH's target audience!), I absolutely hated it where this book was concerned. I felt like it was too easy to miss the gems hidden within or to really understand the progression of his life and works and learnings. It was too hard for me to choose my own adventure and not get lost; a choose-your-own-adventure book doesn't work too well with reality, which was very hard to find and follow amongst the overreaching adventure scenarios. At one point, I tried to just read it straight through, skipping the obviously made-up parts so I could at least finish it and have some idea of his life. I made it to about page 120, and then I gave up.<br /><br />More importantly, however, now that I've had time to think on it, what bothered me more was that I felt this format took an amazing life filled with wisdom, love, and discoveries... and turned it into one big joke. I get it, NPH is a comedian, a showman, so something like that is expected. But I enjoyed the laughs that were weaved into his stories and writing so much because they added to it, whereas the ultimate "joke" of the format untangled all that. It reads like Neil Patrick Harris wanted to write an autobiography, but was frightened of how vulnerable it would make him, so he hid behind two layers of comedy, one of which works really well and the other of which doesn't work at all. It almost made it painful to read in a way, uncomfortable, like that through his avoidance to tell the story in a linear fashion and despite the overall positivity the words bring, I was witnessing some inner-turmoil that I shouldn't be seeing and that still hasn't been resolved. I am probably reading way too much into it, but I also can't change the fact that that is how I felt reading this. I think this book is more emotional than people realize.<br /><br />Lastly, I felt like a book like this would be virtually impossible to enjoy on a Kindle, particularly where using it in the intended way comes into play, so I shelled out $25 or whatever for the hardcover, which I deeply regret.<br /><br />So, one star for the fact that I couldn't finish it due to the format + five stars for the writing and non-made-up content = a 3-star book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14535355528853518887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1068264913" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" href="/user/show/1379514-magdalena-aka-a-bookaholic-swede">Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer15719124437226279260">Have I read the whole book? I don't think so! Why not you ask me? Well, it's because in this book you will have to pick your own way to get to the end/endings. Which means that I have read the book, jumping around, precisely like the old adventure books my brother had when I was younger. You haven't read an adventure book where you have to pick your own way? Then I feel sorry for you, they are great, I wish I had one of them right now (well if I had one I would probably just cheat to get to the </span>
  <span id="freeText15719124437226279260" style="display:none">Have I read the whole book? I don't think so! Why not you ask me? Well, it's because in this book you will have to pick your own way to get to the end/endings. Which means that I have read the book, jumping around, precisely like the old adventure books my brother had when I was younger. You haven't read an adventure book where you have to pick your own way? Then I feel sorry for you, they are great, I wish I had one of them right now (well if I had one I would probably just cheat to get to the ending). So there is probably parts of the book that I have missed, but that is part of the fun. The next time I pick up the book, I could very well find a hidden gem, that I missed the last time.<br><br>Anyway, got sidetracked a bit. This is a great book. I had a lot of fun jumping here and there, reading about NPH life. He's such a great guy. The kind you really, really would love to have as a friend. This is one of the best autobiographies I have read, not only because it is different, but because it's interesting and funny.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415610868ra/11818197.gif" alt="" width="400" height="180" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><em>I received the book from <a href="http://www.bloggingforbooks.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blogging for Books</a> in exchange for an honest review.</em></span>

<div id="review_1192486864" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1192486864" />
    <a title="Barbara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2172096-barbara"><img alt="Barbara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598060221p2/2172096.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1192486864?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara" href="/user/show/2172096-barbara">Barbara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1192486864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11092871893359814565">Neil Patrick Harris is an American actor, writer, producer, singer, and magician. <br/><br/><img alt='' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1535249787i/26200504.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>*****<br/><br/>I listened to the audio version of this book, read by the author. The book takes us from Harris's childhood with a loving, supportive family in New Mexico to his current mega-success in show business and his happy home life. <br/> <br/>Harris developed his love of performing as a child and started his acting career at a young age. He also developed an early interest in magic, which he studied seriously, and he includes </span>
  <span id="freeText11092871893359814565" style="display:none">Neil Patrick Harris is an American actor, writer, producer, singer, and magician. <br><br><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1535249787i/26200504.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*****<br><br>I listened to the audio version of this book, read by the author. The book takes us from Harris's childhood with a loving, supportive family in New Mexico to his current mega-success in show business and his happy home life. <br> <br>Harris developed his love of performing as a child and started his acting career at a young age. He also developed an early interest in magic, which he studied seriously, and he includes some nifty card tricks in the book. Harris seems to have had few 'lows' in his career. In addition to two successful TV series ('Doogie Howser, M.D'. and 'How I Met Your Mother') and a Netflix show ('A Series of Unfortunate Events'), he starred in theatrical productions, did guest spots on TV series, starred in TV movies, had parts in big-screen films, hosted award shows, starred in popular YouTube series, and is now a successful author.<br><br><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1535248991i/26200450.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Neil Patrick Harris as Doogie Howser, M.D.</b><br><br><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1535249787i/26200506.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Neil Patrick Harris as Count Olaf in A Series of Unfortunate Events</b><br><br>Harris's stories about his career - and his co-stars, directors, and people he worked with - are generally rendered in an upbeat, positive tone (the book is not a mean-spirited tell-all). While detailing his many successes Harris never comes across as arrogant but rather as a talented, hard-working guy who's had some good luck. Harris is also a keen student of the 'behind the scenes' aspects of show business and likes to go backstage, shadow the director, study how shots are set up, etc. <br><br>One of the most detailed stories in the book is about Harris's starring role in the Broadway production of "Hedwig and the Angry Inch." It's interesting to see how he got the role, prepared for the part, and was able to do eight shows per week while juggling other responsibilities. Harris also describes how he and the writers prepared musical numbers when he hosted award shows like the Tony Awards and the Oscars - a feat that was very creative and entertaining. <br><br><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1535248991i/26200452.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1535249787i/26200505.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <b>Neil Patrick Harris in Hedwig and the Angry Inch. He won a Tony Award for 'Best Actor in a Musical'</b><br><br>Harris talks openly about his sexuality. As a youngster he had girlfriends, apparently not quite realizing (or admitting to himself) that he was gay. Afterwards Harris was publicly silent about his sexuality until circumstances forced him to come out - which he did in a graceful, carefully crafted statement. Harris's tale about meeting the love of his life - actor/writer David Burtka - is engaging, as is the story of their becoming parents to two children (via egg donor and surrogate). <br><br><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1535249787i/26200507.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Neil Patrick Harris and David Burtka</b><br><br><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1535248991i/26200451.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>David Burtka and Neil Patrick Harris with their children Harper Grace and Gideon</b><br><br>Another story describes how Harris and Burtka became close friends with Elton John and his husband David Furnish. The lucky Harris/Burtka household gets to ride in private planes and visit Elton John's mansion in England - complete with pampering household staff and wonderful food.<br> <br>The book isn't a text on how to succeed in show business but rather a wide (though not always deep) overview of Harris's life and career. I thought it was well-written and interesting. The 'alternate life stories' (fictional) are humorous, though some are gritty and end badly. Overall, I liked the book. Neil Patrick Harris fans will probably enjoy it.<br><br>You can follow my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot.com/">https://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot....</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11092871893359814565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TL " class="user" itemprop="url" name="TL " href="/user/show/4342402-tl">TL </a>

<span id="freeTextContainer13731542328268377822">4.5 stars:)<br/><br/>I don't remember who recced this to me... I remember seeing this pop up on my feed alot at one point and getting curious so I added it to my amazon wishlist and forgot about it for awhile.   <span id="freeText13731542328268377822" style="display:none">4.5 stars:)<br /><br />I don't remember who recced this to me... I remember seeing this pop up on my feed alot at one point and getting curious so I added it to my amazon wishlist and forgot about it for awhile. Then I got Alan Cumming's beautiful memoir in the mail and remembered this one. <br /><br />I went to buy it and noticed that there was an audiobook as well. Curious to see how the book's format would translate I got that instead of the hardcover. <br /><br />Confession: I knew about Neil before but not very much. I was excited but a little apprehensive as well, sometimes autobiography/biography and me don't get along.<br /><br />Right from the start, Neil put a smile on my face and had me laughing along with some of the stories.<br /><br />At times touching/sweet/hilarious, he pulls you in and doesn't let go. It's like you are sitting there with him, curled up with your favorite drink.<br /><br />The section where David came in and talked along with Neil was one of my favorites, I could just imagine them having so much fun and big smiles on their faces. I wanted to hug the stuffing out of them:).<br /><br />I would highly recommend, it's inspired me to look up more of Neil's work (heck knows when I'll get to it haha but I shall!).<br /><br />He's had such an interesting life and like Alan and also John Barrowman, is a very lovely person. <br /><br />Happy reading! <br /><br />P.S. The audiobook handles the 'choose your own autobiography' version very well. It just goes through each track with sayings like "keep listening", "hold on it's coming" among others. <br /><br />Excuse any typos for now, doing this via phone </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15760645144468668007">I fell in love with Neil Patrick Harris when he was on "How I Met Your Mother" and this "memoir" just nailed that fact home. This would have been really cool to actually read since it's written in a Choose Your Own Adventure format, but I couldn't pass up listening to this narrated by NPH himself. And it worked, it was great!<br/><br/>Basically the idea is that this autobiography is about you - you get to live his life and choose how to proceed with possible alternatives. It's funny and packed with inform</span>
  <span id="freeText15760645144468668007" style="display:none">I fell in love with Neil Patrick Harris when he was on "How I Met Your Mother" and this "memoir" just nailed that fact home. This would have been really cool to actually read since it's written in a Choose Your Own Adventure format, but I couldn't pass up listening to this narrated by NPH himself. And it worked, it was great!<br /><br />Basically the idea is that this autobiography is about you - you get to live his life and choose how to proceed with possible alternatives. It's funny and packed with information I never knew about him. 5 Stars!</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1080646118" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15350239269475749117"><b>Actual Rating 3.5<br/><br/>I grew up watching Doogie Howser, M.D. reruns, and have spent the last nine years waiting for more episodes of How I Met Your Mother to watch, often over and over again, but I knew little about Neil Patrick Harris’ personal life.</b> I knew about David and Harper and Gideon, but not how NPH had come out, how he had met his husband, or about how he knew he was born to entertain from a very early age. Nor did I realise that he’s a magician, and Barney Stinson’s adventures in magic mus</span>
  <span id="freeText15350239269475749117" style="display:none"><b>Actual Rating 3.5<br /><br />I grew up watching Doogie Howser, M.D. reruns, and have spent the last nine years waiting for more episodes of How I Met Your Mother to watch, often over and over again, but I knew little about Neil Patrick Harris’ personal life.</b> I knew about David and Harper and Gideon, but not how NPH had come out, how he had met his husband, or about how he knew he was born to entertain from a very early age. Nor did I realise that he’s a magician, and Barney Stinson’s adventures in magic must have come from Neil, rather than the producers or writers of the show.<br /><br />While I feel like Neil Patrick Harris is one of only a few celebrities who could get away with a Choose Your Own Autobiography, and while I absolutely ADORED reading Choose Your Own Adventure books when I was younger, I can’t help but feel I lost a lot of information in this unique style of telling.<br /><br /><b>The rest of this review can be found <a href="http://magazine.100percentrock.com/reviews/book-reviews/201412/91382" rel="nofollow noopener">here!</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15350239269475749117" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <a title="Sesana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sesana" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana">Sesana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=memoir">memoir</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1091226092" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11890002812031088437">There are two ways to read this (one of a kind?) choose-your-own-adventure style biography, and I did both. You can either do the choose-your-own adventure team, either playing around with the format (there are several authentically horrible deaths) or just reading the parts you're interested in. Want to concentrate on NPH's magic? Sure! The musicals? Done! You can also read the book straight through, which is actually somewhat less confusing than it sounds. You'll go through his life in somewha</span>
  <span id="freeText11890002812031088437" style="display:none">There are two ways to read this (one of a kind?) choose-your-own-adventure style biography, and I did both. You can either do the choose-your-own adventure team, either playing around with the format (there are several authentically horrible deaths) or just reading the parts you're interested in. Want to concentrate on NPH's magic? Sure! The musicals? Done! You can also read the book straight through, which is actually somewhat less confusing than it sounds. You'll go through his life in somewhat chronological order, with the exception of a few odd pages of magic tricks, cocktail recipes, and the aforementioned horrible deaths.<br /><br />If you're already a longtime fan of NPH, you won't be learning much new. So if you have, for example, had a huge crush on him since you were in elementary school and he was Doogie. Just as an example. But it is still fun to read it all at once, with his thoughts. Which does, indeed, make it a fans-only type of book. But surely you expected that anyways, right? No, you won't learn much new here. I already knew about his Broadway career, his family, and that Dustin Diamond is an ass. The one thing that did stand out to me is how much NPH loves and feels grateful for his family, which is nice if undramatic to read about.<br /><br />Not a particularly juicy memoir, it's true, but it is fun to read, especially for somebody who's been a fan for a long time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11890002812031088437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1085619134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9007988442820107026">This book beautifully explains what make Harris such a marvelous performer: he is singularly focused on providing the most entertaining performance possible. Here he's made the actor memoir into a delightfully entertaining book. It's not because he's had such a fascinating life, although it's been a pleasant one, full of rewarding work from an early age, and it's not because he spills a lot of secrets. Mostly you walk away from this thinking what a devoted family man he is and how much he enjoys</span>
  <span id="freeText9007988442820107026" style="display:none">This book beautifully explains what make Harris such a marvelous performer: he is singularly focused on providing the most entertaining performance possible. Here he's made the actor memoir into a delightfully entertaining book. It's not because he's had such a fascinating life, although it's been a pleasant one, full of rewarding work from an early age, and it's not because he spills a lot of secrets. Mostly you walk away from this thinking what a devoted family man he is and how much he enjoys his work.<br /><br />Very nearly pure fun.<br /><br />Library copy</span>

<div id="review_950047483" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/950047483" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9978483-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524369713p2/9978483.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/950047483?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/9978483-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9978483-matthew?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9978483-matthew?shelf=m-m">m-m</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9978483-matthew?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9978483-matthew?shelf=autobiography">autobiography</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9978483-matthew?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9978483-matthew?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9978483-matthew?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9978483-matthew?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9978483-matthew?shelf=adults">adults</a>,
